I am designing a local AI-assisted research and backtesting system to help me develop and iterate on systematic trading strategies in Python. The goal is to build a tool that accelerates research, enforces disciplined evaluation, and remains fully under my control.
The system should be structured with two cooperating AI components:
1. Strategy Backtester Agent
   * Accepts a Python trading algorithm I have written.
   * Performs backtests across multiple asset classes, including:
      * Major and minor Forex pairs
      * Cryptocurrency markets
      * Futures contracts
      * Equities with optional stock screening support
   * Uses realistic historical data including adjustable:
      * Fees
      * Slippage
      * Bid/ask spreads
   * Produces standardized, quantitative performance metrics such as:
      * CAGR
      * Sharpe ratio
      * Maximum drawdown
      * Win rate
      * Expectancy
      * Trade count
   * Generates structured outputs (CSV/JSON/DB) that can be programmatically compared.
2. Strategy Mutation & Suggestion Agent
   * Uses a configurable library of strategy components (e.g., indicators, entry/exit rules, filters, risk modules) that I can edit and expand.
   * Takes a base strategy and programmatically generates variants such as:
      * Adding or replacing indicators (e.g., “add ADX confirmation,” “use ATR stop instead of fixed stop”)
      * Modifying parameters within bounded ranges
      * Combining rules from the component library
   * Submits each variant to the Strategy Backtester Agent for evaluation.
   * Helps summarize differences between variants and highlights statistically meaningful changes.
Both AI agents should operate locally or on my own hardware. The Strategy Mutation Agent should never execute backtests directly—it should only generate structured strategy specifications that the Backtester runs deterministically.
I also want detailed, objective research on the following:
* Which local large language models (LLMs) are most suitable for each agent’s role (code generation vs. research summarization vs. explanation), including performance characteristics and limitations.
* Hardware requirements for running these local models efficiently (CPU/GPU options, memory, storage), with recommendations for:
   * Minimum cost / budget setup
   * Recommended balanced setup
   * High-performance setup
* Price estimates for each setup, including:
   * Cost of acquiring hardware
   * Cost of any required software or paid LLM licenses (if applicable)
   * Expected ongoing costs (electricity, local compute maintenance)
Your response should:
* Propose a clear system architecture showing how the two agents, data storage, and the backtesting engine interact.
* Recommend specific local LLM models for each role with pros/cons and why they fit that purpose.
* Provide hardware configurations in detail at three price tiers (budget, recommended, high-end).
* Explain how to structure and maintain the strategy component library so it remains:
   * Editable by me
   * Interpretable
   * Constrained to prevent nonsensical mutations
* Include examples of how the agents would process a strategy and generate a variant for testing.
The overarching goal is to create a local research assistant that:
* Keeps me in control of all code and data
* Produces reproducible, realistic backtest results
* Helps automate and accelerate systematic strategy iteration
* Does not rely on black-box trading advice                                                                                               
I also have a pasted file from chat gpt of ideas on how this could work. If you think you could do better then do it. You can use it for advise or improve on it, as long as the best item comes out in the end. Thanks.Show moreJan 7Comprehensive AI-Assisted Trading Strategy Research System
I'll design an enhanced, production-ready system that improves on the provided architecture while maintaining your core requirements for local control, reproducibility, and systematic iteration.
Executive Summary
This system separates strategic creativity (Mutation Agent) from empirical truth (Backtester Agent), ensuring that no AI hallucinates performance metrics and all results are deterministically reproducible. The architecture prioritizes data provenance, statistical rigor, and iterative improvement over raw speed.

1. Enhanced System Architecture
Core Design Principles

Separation of Concerns: Mutation Agent proposes ideas; Backtester Agent measures reality
Zero Trust Execution: All LLM outputs are validated before execution
Full Auditability: Every result ties to exact code, data, and model versions
Human-in-the-Loop: Critical decisions (parameter bounds, component approvals) remain under your control
Statistical Rigor: Built-in safeguards against overfitting and data snooping

2. Recommended Local LLM Models
Strategy Mutation Agent (Creative Reasoning)
Primary Recommendation: Qwen2.5-Coder 32B Instruct

Strengths:

Exceptional code understanding and generation
Strong reasoning about algorithmic logic
Excellent instruction following for structured outputs
Good at maintaining constraints (parameter bounds, compatibility)
Supports large context windows (32K+ tokens)


Quantization: Use Q5_K_M for best quality/speed balance
VRAM Required: ~22GB (Q5_K_M), ~18GB (Q4_K_M)
Why for Mutation Agent: Understands trading logic, generates valid Python/JSON, respects constraints

Alternative: DeepSeek-Coder-V2 16B

Strengths: Similar code capabilities, lower memory footprint (~12GB Q5_K_M)
Trade-off: Slightly less sophisticated reasoning for complex mutations
Best for: Budget setups or when running both agents simultaneously

Alternative: Llama 3.1 70B Instruct (High-end only)

Strengths: Superior reasoning, better at complex hypothesis generation
Trade-off: Requires 48GB+ VRAM, slower inference
Best for: Maximum quality, multi-step reasoning about strategy behavior

Strategy Backtester Agent (Orchestration & Explanation)
Primary Recommendation: Qwen2.5 14B Instruct

Strengths:

Strong instruction following
Good at coordinating multi-step processes
Excellent at generating clear explanations
Lower resource requirements (~10GB Q5_K_M)


Why for Backtester: Most work is deterministic Python; LLM only orchestrates and explains

Alternative: Mistral-Nemo 12B Instruct

Strengths: Very efficient, strong reasoning, good context handling
Trade-off: Slightly less precise with technical terminology
Best for: Budget setups where Backtester role is minimal

Alternative: Llama 3.3 70B Instruct (High-end)

Strengths: Best-in-class explanation quality, debugging insights
Best for: When you want detailed analysis of backtest failures or anomalies

Component Schema (Example: RSI Indicator)
yaml# indicators/momentum/rsi.yaml

metadata:
  name: "Relative Strength Index"
  category: "momentum"
  subcategory: "oscillator"
  version: "1.0.0"
  author: "J. Welles Wilder"
  description: "Measures momentum via ratio of up/down closes over period"
  
parameters:
  period:
    type: "integer"
    default: 14
    min: 2
    max: 100
    recommended_range: [10, 30]
    description: "Lookback period for RSI calculation"
    rationale: "Shorter = more responsive but noisy; longer = smoother but laggy"
    
  overbought:
    type: "float"
    default: 70.0
    min: 50.0
    max: 90.0
    recommended_range: [65, 80]
    description: "Threshold for overbought condition"
    
  oversold:
    type: "float"
    default: 30.0
    min: 10.0
    max: 50.0
    recommended_range: [20, 35]
    description: "Threshold for oversold condition"

requirements:
  data:
    - "close"
  minimum_bars: 100  # At least 100 bars for stable calculation
  
compatibility:
  assets:
    - "forex"
    - "crypto"
    - "futures"
    - "equities"
  timeframes:
    - "1m"
    - "5m"
    - "15m"
    - "1h"
    - "4h"
    - "1d"
  restrictions:
    - "Not suitable for ultra-low volume assets"
    - "May produce false signals in strong trends"

implementation:
  file: "implementations/indicators.py"
  function: "calculate_rsi"
  dependencies:
    - "pandas"
    - "numpy"
    - "ta-lib"  # optional, faster

statistical_properties:
  lookback_bars: 
    formula: "period + 1"
  lag_bars: 1
  sensitivity: "medium"
  stability: "high"
  
usage_examples:
  - entry_signal: "rsi < oversold"
    description: "Enter long when oversold"
  - exit_signal: "rsi > overbought"
    description: "Exit long when overbought"
  - filter: "rsi > 50"
    description: "Trend strength filter (bullish bias)"

mutation_hints:
  - "Try period in range [8, 21] for different responsiveness"
  - "Combine with trend filter to reduce false signals"
  - "Use divergence detection for advanced entries"
  - "Consider different thresholds for different assets"

research_notes:
  - "Original paper: Wilder (1978), New Concepts in Technical Trading Systems"
  - "Commonly overfit when optimized independently"
  - "More effective as a filter than a primary signal"
Component Compatibility Matrix
yaml# validation/compatibility_matrix.yaml

# Define which combinations are valid/invalid

valid_combinations:
  - name: "Trend Following with ADX Filter"
    components:
      entry: ["crossover"]
      filters: ["adx_trend_strength"]
      exit: ["atr_stop", "trailing_stop"]
    rationale: "ADX confirms trend strength for crossover systems"
    
  - name: "Mean Reversion with Volatility Filter"
    components:
      entry: ["oversold_bounce"]
      filters: ["volatility_filter"]
      exit: ["risk_reward", "time_stop"]
    rationale: "Mean reversion works best in stable volatility regimes"

invalid_combinations:
  - name: "Conflicting Entry Logic"
    components:
      entry: ["breakout", "oversold_bounce"]
    reason: "Trend-following and mean-reversion are contradictory"
    severity: "error"
    
  - name: "Redundant Indicators"
    components:
      indicators: ["rsi", "stochastic"]
    reason: "Both measure similar momentum; likely correlated"
    severity: "warning"
    
  - name: "Incompatible Timeframes"
    components:
      entry: ["vwap_cross"]
      timeframe: ["1d"]
    reason: "VWAP requires intraday data"
    severity: "error"

parameter_interactions:
  - components: ["atr_stop", "atr_target"]
    constraint: "target_multiplier > stop_multiplier"
    reason: "Risk-reward ratio must be positive"
    
  - components: ["sma_short", "sma_long"]
    constraint: "short_period < long_period"
    reason: "Short MA must be faster than long MA"
Constraint Rules Engine
yaml# validation/constraint_rules.yaml

global_constraints:
  max_indicators: 5
  max_filters: 3
  max_lookback_bars: 500  # Prevent excessive lag
  min_trades_expected: 200  # Minimum for statistical significance
  
asset_specific:
  forex:
    min_timeframe: "1m"
    max_spread_pips: 5
    session_restrictions: ["no_news_releases"]
    
  crypto:
    min_timeframe: "1m"
    volatility_limits:
      min_daily: 0.001  # 0.1%
      max_daily: 0.50   # 50%
      
  equities:
    min_timeframe: "1d"
    requires: ["survivorship_bias_free_data"]
    restrictions: ["no_penny_stocks"]

research_constraints:
  walk_forward:
    in_sample_ratio: 0.7
    out_of_sample_ratio: 0.3
    min_oos_trades: 50
    
  parameter_stability:
    test_range: 0.2  # +/- 20% from optimal
    min_performance_ratio: 0.7  # OOS must be 70%+ of IS
    
  statistical_tests:
    - "sharpe_ratio > 1.0"
    - "win_rate > 0.35"
    - "profit_factor > 1.3"
    - "max_drawdown < 0.25"

Mutation Agent Prompt TemplateMutation Agent System PromptCode """
MUTATION AGENT SYSTEM PROMPT
============================

ROLE:
You are a systematic trading strategy research assistant specialized in 
generating testable variants of trading algorithms. Your purpose is to 
propose minimal, interpretable modifI'm finally starting this project. My gpu is a nvidia Geforce RTX 2080 super. can i run any of the models lsitedJan 11not in the provided library

All parameter values must fall within defined bounds
Provide specific hypotheses, not vague improvements

OUTPUT SCHEMA:

"metrics": ["max_drawdown", "win_rate"],

"confidence": "medium"
},
"rationale": "Research shows volatility-adjusted stops reduce tail risk in trending markets",
"tags": ["risk_management", "stop_optimization"]
}
MUTATION STRATEGIES:

Parameter Perturbation:

Adjust single parameter within bounds
Test boundaries (min, max, default +/- 20%)
Use economically meaningful values (round numbers, common periods)


Component Addition:

Add one filter to reduce false signals
Add one confirmation indicator
Ensure compatibility with existing components


Component Replacement:

Swap similar components (e.g., RSI → Stochastic)
Maintain logical consistency
Preserve mutation distance (don't change strategy type)


Multi-Component Interaction:

Test parameter combinations (e.g., stop AND target)
Only when theoretically justified
Maximum 2 simultaneous changes



HYPOTHESIS QUALITY:
Good: "Tighter stop with wider target (1.5:3.0 RR) will improve profit factor
by cutting losses faster while allowing trends to run"
Bad:  "This will make the strategy better"
EXAMPLE INTERACTION:

Phase 5: Build Your First Component - The Backtester Agent
Now we start building! Don't worry, I'll provide all the code and explain what it does.
Step 5.1: Create the basic strategy structure
Open Notepad and create a new file called simple_strategy.py:
python# simple_strategy.py
# This is your first trading strategy - a simple moving average crossover

import backtrader as bt

class SimpleMovingAverageCrossover(bt.Strategy):
    """
    A basic strategy that:
    1. Buys when a fast moving average crosses above a slow moving average
    2. Sells when the fast crosses below the slow
    """
    
    params = (
        ('fast_period', 10),  # Fast moving average (10 days)
        ('slow_period', 30),  # Slow moving average (30 days)
    )
    
    def __init__(self):
        # Create the two moving averages
        self.fast_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.fast_period
        )
        self.slow_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.slow_period
        )
        
        # Create a crossover signal
        self.crossover = bt.indicators.CrossOver(self.fast_ma, self.slow_ma)
    
    def next(self):
        # This function runs every day
        
        if not self.position:  # If we don't have a position
            if self.crossover > 0:  # If fast MA crossed above slow MA
                self.buy()  # Buy!
        
        else:  # If we do have a position
            if self.crossover < 0:  # If fast MA crossed below slow MA
                self.sell()  # Sell!
Save this in C:\TradingResearch\strategies\simple_strategy.py
What does this code do?

It defines a simple trading strategy
It uses two moving averages (averages of past prices)
When the fast average crosses above the slow one = BUY signal
When the fast average crosses below the slow one = SELL signal


Step 5.2: Create the Backtester
Now create a file called backtester.py:
python# backtester.py
# This runs your strategy on historical data to see how it would have performed

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
from datetime import datetime
import pandas as pd

class StrategyBacktester:
    """
    This class runs your trading strategies on historical data
    """
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.results = {}
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=10000, commission=0.001):
        """
        Run a backtest on one stock/asset
        
        Parameters:
        - strategy_class: The strategy to test (e.g., SimpleMovingAverageCrossover)
        - symbol: Stock symbol (e.g., 'AAPL' for Apple)
        - start_date: When to start the test (e.g., '2020-01-01')
        - end_date: When to end the test (e.g., '2023-12-31')
        - initial_cash: Starting money (default: $10,000)
        - commission: Trading fee (default: 0.1%)
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"Running backtest for {symbol}")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"Initial Cash: ${initial_cash:,.2f}")
        print(f"{'='*60}\n")
        
        # Step 1: Download historical data
        print(f"Downloading data for {symbol}...")
        data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"ERROR: No data found for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        print(f"✓ Downloaded {len(data)} days of data")
        
        # Step 2: Create a backtrader engine
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Step 3: Add the data
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(dataname=data)
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Step 4: Add the strategy
        cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Step 5: Set starting cash
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        
        # Step 6: Set commission (trading fees)
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Step 7: Add analyzers (calculate performance metrics)
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.Returns, _name='returns')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        
        # Step 8: Run the backtest!
        print("\nRunning backtest...")
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        results = cerebro.run()
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Step 9: Extract results
        strat = results[0]
        
        # Get metrics
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        returns = strat.analyzers.returns.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate additional metrics
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        
        # Print results
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"BACKTEST RESULTS FOR {symbol}")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        print(f"Starting Portfolio Value:  ${starting_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Ending Portfolio Value:    ${ending_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Total Return:              {total_return:.2f}%")
        print(f"Sharpe Ratio:              {sharpe.get('sharperatio', 'N/A')}")
        print(f"Max Drawdown:              {drawdown.max.drawdown:.2f}%")
        print(f"Total Trades:              {trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0}")
        
        if trades.total.closed and trades.total.closed > 0:
            win_rate = (trades.won.total / trades.total.closed) * 100
            print(f"Win Rate:                  {win_rate:.2f}%")
        
        print(f"{'='*60}\n")
        
        # Store results
        result_dict = {
            'symbol': symbol,
            'start_date': start_date,
            'end_date': end_date,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio', None),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0,
        }
        
        return result_dict
Save this as C:\TradingResearch\backtester.py

Break-Even Analysis
When does local become cheaper than API?
Let's calculate:
Scenario: $100/month Claude API usage
RTX 4060 Ti ($650 + $35/month electricity):

Month 1-6: Losing (you spent $650 + $210 = $860 vs. $600 API)
Month 7-12: Breaking even ($860 + $210 = $1,070 vs. $1,200 API)
Break-even: ~9 months
After 2 years: $1,490 local vs. $2,400 API (save $910)

RTX 4090 ($2,000 + $70/month electricity):

Month 1-12: Losing ($2,000 + $840 = $2,840 vs. $1,200 API)
Month 13-24: Breaking even ($2,840 + $840 = $3,680 vs. $2,400 API)
Break-even: ~16 months
After 2 years: $3,680 local vs. $2,400 API (lose $1,280)
After 3 years: $5,200 local vs. $3,600 API (lose $1,600)

Conclusion: For $100/month usage, RTX 4090 NEVER pays for itself vs. Claude API

You'll break even in 12 months

Important Clarification: You're NOT Training AI
I need to correct something important:

"would it be cheaper to pay for claude and train an ai on there"

You are NOT training AI models in this project. This is a huge misconception that will save you tons of money!
What you're actually doing:

Using pre-trained models (either Claude API or local models like DeepSeek)
Asking them to generate strategy variants and analyze results
The models already know how to code and reason - you're just prompting them

Training an AI model would cost:

Hundreds of thousands to millions of dollars
Requires massive datasets
Needs specialized hardware (A100/H100 GPUs)
Takes weeks/months

What you're doing costs:

$100-200/month (API) or $2,000 one-time (local hardware)
Uses models others trained
Takes seconds per request
This is called "inference" not "training"

That's it! Should we do this now?Alright, we're going to get claude then and run it like that. Should I start with the backtest agent or the strategy mutation and suggestion agent firstJan 11Start with the Backtester Agent First - Here's Why
Excellent question! You should definitely start with the Backtester Agent first. Here's the logical reasoning:
Why Backtester Agent First?
1. You Need a Working Foundation
Think of it like building a house:

Backtester Agent = The foundation and measuring tools
Mutation Agent = The architect suggesting renovations

You can't evaluate suggestions if you don't have a reliable way to test them!
2. Validates Your System Works
Before AI starts generating 100 strategy variants, you need to know:

✅ Does your backtesting actually work?
✅ Are the results accurate and reproducible?
✅ Can you trust the metrics?
✅ Is your data quality good?

3. Gives You Baseline Results
You need to test your simple strategy first to:

Understand what "good" results look like
Learn what metrics matter for your trading style
Build intuition about strategy performance
Have something to compare mutations against

4. Simpler Integration
The Backtester Agent's AI role is simpler:

Takes backtest results → Explains them in plain English
Identifies patterns in performance
Suggests what might be wrong

The Mutation Agent is more complex (generates new code/specs).
5. Immediate Value
Even without mutations, the Backtester Agent helps you:

Understand why strategies fail/succeed
Learn from results faster
Document your research automatically


The Build Order
Phase 1: Basic Backtester (✅ You already did this!)
   └─> Can run backtests on one strategy, one asset

Phase 2: Enhanced Backtester + Claude Integration (👈 START HERE)
   └─> Add multi-asset testing
   └─> Add results database
   └─> Integrate Claude for analysis
   └─> Test thoroughly with manual strategy variants

Phase 3: Strategy Mutation Agent (Later)
   └─> Build component library
   └─> Add Claude-powered mutation generation
   └─> Connect to validated backtester

Step 4: Create the Results Database
Create database.py:
python# database.py
# Handles storing and retrieving backtest results

import sqlite3
import json
from datetime import datetime
import config

class ResultsDatabase:
    """
    Stores all backtest results in a SQLite database
    """
    
    def __init__(self, db_path=config.DATABASE_PATH):
        self.db_path = db_path
        self.init_database()
    
    def init_database(self):
        """Create tables if they don't exist"""
        conn = sqlite3.connect(self.db_path)
        cursor = conn.cursor()
        
        # Create backtests table
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS backtests (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                strategy_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                symbol TEXT NOT NULL,
                start_date TEXT NOT NULL,
                end_date TEXT NOT NULL,
                initial_cash REAL,
                final_value REAL,
                total_return_pct REAL,
                sharpe_ratio REAL,
                max_drawdown_pct REAL,
                total_trades INTEGER,
                win_rate REAL,
                profit_factor REAL,
                strategy_params TEXT,
                timestamp TEXT NOT NULL,
                claude_analysis TEXT
            )
        ''')
        
        conn.commit()
        conn.close()
        print(f"✓ Database initialized at {self.db_path}")
    
    def save_backtest(self, result):
        """Save a backtest result to the database"""
        conn = sqlite3.connect(self.db_path)
        cursor = conn.cursor()
        
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO backtests (
                strategy_name, symbol, start_date, end_date,
                initial_cash, final_value, total_return_pct,
                sharpe_ratio, max_drawdown_pct, total_trades,
                win_rate, profit_factor, strategy_params,
                timestamp, claude_analysis
            ) VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
        ''', (
            result.get('strategy_name'),
            result.get('symbol'),
            result.get('start_date'),
            result.get('end_date'),
            result.get('starting_value'),
            result.get('ending_value'),
            result.get('total_return_pct'),
            result.get('sharpe_ratio'),
            result.get('max_drawdown_pct'),
            result.get('total_trades'),
            result.get('win_rate'),
            result.get('profit_factor'),
            json.dumps(result.get('strategy_params', {})),
            datetime.now().isoformat(),
            result.get('claude_analysis', '')
        ))
        
        backtest_id = cursor.lastrowid
        conn.commit()
        conn.close()
        
        return backtest_id
    
    def get_all_backtests(self, strategy_name=None, symbol=None):
        """Retrieve backtests with optional filtering"""
        conn = sqlite3.connect(self.db_path)
        cursor = conn.cursor()
        
        query = "SELECT * FROM backtests WHERE 1=1"
        params = []
        
        if strategy_name:
            query += " AND strategy_name = ?"
            params.append(strategy_name)
        
        if symbol:
            query += " AND symbol = ?"
            params.append(symbol)
        
        query += " ORDER BY timestamp DESC"
        
        cursor.execute(query, params)
        results = cursor.fetchall()
        conn.close()
        
        return results
    
    def get_backtest_summary(self):
        """Get summary statistics across all backtests"""
        conn = sqlite3.connect(self.db_path)
        cursor = conn.cursor()
        
        cursor.execute('''
            SELECT 
                COUNT(*) as total_backtests,
                COUNT(DISTINCT strategy_name) as unique_strategies,
                COUNT(DISTINCT symbol) as unique_symbols,
                AVG(total_return_pct) as avg_return,
                AVG(sharpe_ratio) as avg_sharpe,
                AVG(max_drawdown_pct) as avg_drawdown
            FROM backtests
        ''')
        
        result = cursor.fetchone()
        conn.close()
        
        return {
            'total_backtests': result[0],
            'unique_strategies': result[1],
            'unique_symbols': result[2],
            'avg_return': result[3],
            'avg_sharpe': result[4],
            'avg_drawdown': result[5]
        }
Save as C:\TradingResearch\database.py
Step 5: Enhanced Backtester with Claude Integration
Now let's upgrade your backtester.py with multi-asset support and Claude analysis:
python# backtester.py (Enhanced Version)
# Now with multi-asset testing and Claude AI analysis

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
from datetime import datetime
import pandas as pd
from anthropic import Anthropic
import json
import config
from database import ResultsDatabase

class StrategyBacktester:
    """
    Enhanced backtester with multi-asset support and AI analysis
    """
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.results = []
        self.db = ResultsDatabase()
        self.claude = Anthropic(api_key=config.CLAUDE_API_KEY)
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=config.DEFAULT_INITIAL_CASH, 
                     commission=config.DEFAULT_COMMISSION,
                     strategy_params=None):
        """
        Run a backtest on one asset
        """
        
        print(f"\nTesting {symbol}...")
        
        # Download data
        data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"❌ No data for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        # Create backtester
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Add data
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(dataname=data)
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Add strategy with parameters
        if strategy_params:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class, **strategy_params)
        else:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Set cash and commission
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Add analyzers
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.Returns, _name='returns')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        
        # Run
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        results = cerebro.run()
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Extract metrics
        strat = results[0]
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        returns = strat.analyzers.returns.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate metrics
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        total_trades = trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0
        win_rate = None
        profit_factor = None
        
        if total_trades > 0:
            win_rate = (trades.won.total / trades.total.closed) * 100 if trades.total.closed else 0
            
            # Calculate profit factor
            gross_profit = trades.won.pnl.total if trades.won.pnl.total else 0
            gross_loss = abs(trades.lost.pnl.total) if trades.lost.pnl.total else 0
            profit_factor = gross_profit / gross_loss if gross_loss > 0 else None
        
        # Build result dictionary
        result = {
            'strategy_name': strategy_class.__name__,
            'symbol': symbol,
            'start_date': start_date,
            'end_date': end_date,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio'),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': total_trades,
            'win_rate': win_rate,
            'profit_factor': profit_factor,
            'strategy_params': strategy_params or {}
        }
        
        print(f"✓ {symbol}: Return={total_return:.2f}%, Trades={total_trades}")
        
        return result
    
    def run_multi_asset_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbols, start_date, end_date,
                                  initial_cash=config.DEFAULT_INITIAL_CASH,
                                  commission=config.DEFAULT_COMMISSION,
                                  strategy_params=None):
        """
        Run backtest across multiple assets
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"MULTI-ASSET BACKTEST")
        print(f"Strategy: {strategy_class.__name__}")
        print(f"Assets: {len(symbols)} symbols")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        
        results = []
        
        for symbol in symbols:
            result = self.run_backtest(
                strategy_class=strategy_class,
                symbol=symbol,
                start_date=start_date,
                end_date=end_date,
                initial_cash=initial_cash,
                commission=commission,
                strategy_params=strategy_params
            )
            
            if result:
                results.append(result)
                # Save to database
                self.db.save_backtest(result)
        
        # Print summary
        self.print_summary(results)
        
        # Get Claude's analysis
        if results:
            print("\n🤖 Asking Claude to analyze results...")
            analysis = self.get_claude_analysis(results, strategy_class.__name__)
            print(f"\n{'='*60}")
            print("CLAUDE'S ANALYSIS:")
            print(f"{'='*60}")
            print(analysis)
            print(f"{'='*60}\n")
        
        return results
    
    def print_summary(self, results):
        """Print summary statistics"""
        if not results:
            print("\n❌ No results to summarize")
            return
        
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print("SUMMARY STATISTICS")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        
        # Calculate averages
        avg_return = sum(r['total_return_pct'] for r in results) / len(results)
        avg_sharpe = sum(r['sharpe_ratio'] for r in results if r['sharpe_ratio']) / len([r for r in results if r['sharpe_ratio']])
        avg_dd = sum(r['max_drawdown_pct'] for r in results) / len(results)
        avg_trades = sum(r['total_trades'] for r in results) / len(results)
        
        positive_returns = len([r for r in results if r['total_return_pct'] > 0])
        
        print(f"Assets Tested:        {len(results)}")
        print(f"Positive Returns:     {positive_returns}/{len(results)} ({positive_returns/len(results)*100:.1f}%)")
        print(f"Average Return:       {avg_return:.2f}%")
        print(f"Average Sharpe:       {avg_sharpe:.2f}")
        print(f"Average Max DD:       {avg_dd:.2f}%")
        print(f"Average Trades:       {avg_trades:.1f}")
        
        # Best and worst performers
        best = max(results, key=lambda x: x['total_return_pct'])
        worst = min(results, key=lambda x: x['total_return_pct'])
        
        print(f"\nBest Performer:       {best['symbol']} ({best['total_return_pct']:.2f}%)")
        print(f"Worst Performer:      {worst['symbol']} ({worst['total_return_pct']:.2f}%)")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
    
    def get_claude_analysis(self, results, strategy_name):
        """
        Use Claude to analyze backtest results
        """
        
        # Prepare results summary for Claude
        summary = {
            'strategy_name': strategy_name,
            'total_assets_tested': len(results),
            'results': []
        }
        
        for r in results:
            summary['results'].append({
                'symbol': r['symbol'],
                'return_pct': round(r['total_return_pct'], 2),
                'sharpe': round(r['sharpe_ratio'], 2) if r['sharpe_ratio'] else None,
                'max_drawdown_pct': round(r['max_drawdown_pct'], 2),
                'trades': r['total_trades'],
                'win_rate': round(r['win_rate'], 2) if r['win_rate'] else None
            })
        
        # Create prompt for Claude
        prompt = f"""I just backtested a trading strategy called "{strategy_name}" across {len(results)} different assets.

Here are the results:

{json.dumps(summary, indent=2)}

Please analyze these results and provide:

1. Overall assessment: Is this strategy promising or not?
2. Performance patterns: Which types of assets performed best/worst?
3. Key concerns: What are the biggest red flags in these results?
4. Specific insights: What do the metrics tell us about the strategy's behavior?
5. Next steps: What should I test or modify next?

Be direct and honest. If the strategy looks bad, say so clearly."""

        # Call Claude API
        try:
            message = self.claude.messages.create(
                model=config.CLAUDE_MODEL,
                max_tokens=2000,
                messages=[{
                    "role": "user",
                    "content": prompt
                }]
            )
            
            analysis = message.content[0].text
            return analysis
            
        except Exception as e:
            return f"Error getting Claude analysis: {str(e)}"
Save this as C:\TradingResearch\backtester.py (replace your old one)
Step 6: Create a New Test Script
Create test_multi_asset.py:
python# test_multi_asset.py
# Test your strategy across multiple assets with Claude analysis

from backtester import StrategyBacktester
from strategies.simple_strategy import SimpleMovingAverageCrossover
import config

# Create the enhanced backtester
backtester = StrategyBacktester()

# Run multi-asset backtest on top 10 stocks
print("Starting multi-asset backtest on major stocks...")

results = backtester.run_multi_asset_backtest(
    strategy_class=SimpleMovingAverageCrossover,
    symbols=config.STOCK_WATCHLIST,

    initial_cash=10000,
    commission=0.001
)

python# simple_strategy.py
# A basic moving average crossover strategy

import backtrader as bt

class SimpleMovingAverageCrossover(bt.Strategy):
    """
    Buy when fast MA crosses above slow MA
    Sell when fast MA crosses below slow MA
    """
    
    params = (
        ('fast_period', 10),
        ('slow_period', 30),
    )
    
    def __init__(self):
        # Calculate two moving averages
        self.fast_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.fast_period
        )
        self.slow_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.slow_period
        )
        
        # Detect when they cross
        self.crossover = bt.indicators.CrossOver(self.fast_ma, self.slow_ma)
    
    def next(self):
        if not self.position:  # Not in the market
            if self.crossover > 0:  # Fast MA crossed above slow MA
                self.buy()
        else:  # In the market
            if self.crossover < 0:  # Fast MA crossed below slow MA
                self.sell()

Name it: simple_strategy.py

Step 4: Create the Basic Backtester

Open Notepad (new file)
Copy this code:

python# backtester.py
# Runs backtests on trading strategies

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
import pandas as pd

class StrategyBacktester:
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=10000, commission=0.001):
        """
        Run a backtest
        
        strategy_class: Your strategy (e.g., SimpleMovingAverageCrossover)
        symbol: Stock ticker (e.g., 'AAPL')
        start_date: Start date (e.g., '2020-01-01')
        end_date: End date (e.g., '2023-12-31')
        initial_cash: Starting money (default $10,000)
        commission: Trading fee (default 0.1%)
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*60}")
        print(f"BACKTEST: {symbol}")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"Starting Cash: ${initial_cash:,.2f}")
        print(f"{'='*60}\n")
        
        # Download data
        print(f"Downloading data for {symbol}...")
        data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"ERROR: Could not download data for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        print(f"✓ Downloaded {len(data)} days of data\n")
        
        # Create backtrader engine
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Add data to engine
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(dataname=data)
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Add strategy
        cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Set starting cash
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        
        # Set commission
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Add performance analyzers
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        
        # Run the backtest
        print("Running backtest...\n")
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        results = cerebro.run()
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Get the strategy results
        strat = results[0]
        
        # Extract metrics
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate return
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        
        # Calculate win rate if there were trades
        total_trades = trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0
        win_rate = None
        if total_trades > 0:
            win_rate = (trades.won.total / trades.total.closed) * 100
        
        # Print results
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        print(f"RESULTS")
        print(f"{'='*60}")
        print(f"Starting Value:     ${starting_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Ending Value:       ${ending_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Total Return:       {total_return:.2f}%")
        print(f"Sharpe Ratio:       {sharpe.get('sharperatio', 'N/A')}")
        print(f"Max Drawdown:       {drawdown.max.drawdown:.2f}%")
        print(f"Total Trades:       {total_trades}")
        if win_rate is not None:
            print(f"Win Rate:           {win_rate:.2f}%")
        print(f"{'='*60}\n")
        
        return {
            'symbol': symbol,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio'),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': total_trades,
            'win_rate': win_rate
        }

Let me clarify the architecture and adjust for your setup.
Answer to Your Key Question
The basic backtest strategy (SimpleMovingAverageCrossover) is just an EXAMPLE to test that everything works.
Here's how it actually works in the full system:
The Three Layers:
1. The Backtesting Engine (Stays the same)

The backtester.py file
This is your "testing machine"
Never changes - it just runs whatever strategy you give it

2. Your Base Strategies (You create these)

These are starting points like simple_strategy.py
You'll have multiple base strategies in your library
Examples:

trend_following_base.py
mean_reversion_base.py
breakout_base.py
momentum_base.py



3. AI-Generated Variants (Automatic)

The Mutation Agent (AI #1) takes a base strategy
Generates variations automatically
Examples from your simple_strategy.py:

Variant 1: Use 10/30 day MAs (original)
Variant 2: Use 10/30 day MAs + ADX filter
Variant 3: Use 15/40 day MAs (different parameters)
Variant 4: Use 10/30 day MAs + RSI confirmation
Variant 5: Use 10/30 day MAs + tighter stop loss



The Workflow:
You write:
   └─> trend_following_base.py (one time)

Mutation Agent generates:
   ├─> variant_001.py (MA 10/30)
   ├─> variant_002.py (MA 10/30 + ADX filter)
   ├─> variant_003.py (MA 15/40)
   ├─> variant_004.py (MA 10/30 + RSI)
   └─> variant_005.py (MA 10/30 + trailing stop)

Backtester Agent tests all of them:
   ├─> Tests variant_001 on 10 stocks
   ├─> Tests variant_002 on 10 stocks
   ├─> Tests variant_003 on 10 stocks
   ├─> Tests variant_004 on 10 stocks
   └─> Tests variant_005 on 10 stocks

Results Database stores everything:
   └─> 50 backtest results (5 variants × 10 stocks)

You review:
   └─> "Variant 2 (MA + ADX) performed best!"
So you write ONE base strategy, and the AI generates dozens/hundreds of variants to test.

python# simple_strategy.py
# This is a BASE STRATEGY - the AI will generate variants from this

import backtrader as bt

class SimpleMovingAverageCrossover(bt.Strategy):
    """
    BASE STRATEGY: Moving Average Crossover
    
    This is your starting point. The Mutation Agent will:
    - Test different MA periods (5/20, 10/30, 20/50, etc.)
    - Add filters (ADX, volatility, volume)
    - Add stops (ATR, percentage, trailing)
    - Add confirmations (RSI, MACD, etc.)
    
    You write this ONCE, AI generates 100s of variants
    """
    
    params = (
        ('fast_period', 10),   # Fast moving average period
        ('slow_period', 30),   # Slow moving average period
    )
    
    def __init__(self):
        # Calculate the two moving averages
        self.fast_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.fast_period
        )
        self.slow_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.slow_period
        )
        
        # Crossover signal
        self.crossover = bt.indicators.CrossOver(self.fast_ma, self.slow_ma)
    
    def next(self):
        # This runs every day/candle
        
        if not self.position:  # Not in a trade
            if self.crossover > 0:  # Fast MA crossed above slow MA
                self.buy()
                
        else:  # In a trade
            if self.crossover < 0:  # Fast MA crossed below slow MA
                self.sell()

New File → Save as D:\TradingResearch\backtester.py
Paste:

python# backtester.py
# The BACKTESTING ENGINE - runs any strategy you give it
# This file stays the same - it's your testing machine

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
import pandas as pd

class StrategyBacktester:
    """
    This is your testing machine.
    
    You give it:
    - A strategy (base or AI-generated variant)
    - A stock/crypto/forex symbol
    - Date range
    
    It gives you back:
    - Performance metrics
    - Trade analysis
    - Risk statistics
    """
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=10000, commission=0.001, strategy_params=None):
        """
        Run a backtest
        
        Parameters:
        -----------
        strategy_class : class
            The strategy to test (e.g., SimpleMovingAverageCrossover)
        symbol : str
            Ticker symbol (e.g., 'AAPL', 'BTC-USD', 'EURUSD=X')
        start_date : str
            Start date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        end_date : str
            End date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        initial_cash : float
            Starting capital (default: $10,000)
        commission : float
            Trading fee per trade (default: 0.1% = 0.001)
        strategy_params : dict
            Custom parameters for the strategy (optional)
        
        Returns:
        --------
        dict : Backtest results with all metrics
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"BACKTESTING: {symbol}")
        print(f"Strategy: {strategy_class.__name__}")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"Starting Capital: ${initial_cash:,.2f}")
        if strategy_params:
            print(f"Parameters: {strategy_params}")
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 1: Download historical data
        print(f"📊 Downloading data for {symbol}...")
        try:
            data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Error downloading data: {e}")
            return None
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"❌ No data found for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        print(f"✓ Downloaded {len(data)} days of data")
        
        # Step 2: Create backtrader engine
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Step 3: Add data
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(dataname=data)
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Step 4: Add strategy (with custom params if provided)
        if strategy_params:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class, **strategy_params)
        else:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Step 5: Configure broker
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Step 6: Add analyzers (calculate performance metrics)
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.Returns, _name='returns')
        
        # Step 7: Run the backtest
        print(f"🔄 Running backtest...")
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        try:
            results = cerebro.run()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Backtest failed: {e}")
            return None
        
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Step 8: Extract results
        strat = results[0]
        
        # Get analyzer results
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        returns = strat.analyzers.returns.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate metrics
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        total_trades = trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0
        
        # Win rate
        win_rate = None
        if total_trades > 0:
            wins = trades.won.total if hasattr(trades, 'won') else 0
            win_rate = (wins / total_trades) * 100
        
        # Profit factor
        profit_factor = None
        if hasattr(trades, 'won') and hasattr(trades, 'lost'):
            gross_profit = trades.won.pnl.total if trades.won.pnl.total else 0
            gross_loss = abs(trades.lost.pnl.total) if trades.lost.pnl.total else 0
            if gross_loss > 0:
                profit_factor = gross_profit / gross_loss
        
        # Step 9: Print results
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"RESULTS FOR {symbol}")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print(f"Starting Portfolio:    ${starting_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Ending Portfolio:      ${ending_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Total Return:          {total_return:+.2f}%")
        print(f"Sharpe Ratio:          {sharpe.get('sharperatio', 'N/A')}")
        print(f"Max Drawdown:          {drawdown.max.drawdown:.2f}%")
        print(f"Total Trades:          {total_trades}")
        
        if win_rate is not None:
            print(f"Win Rate:              {win_rate:.2f}%")
        if profit_factor is not None:
            print(f"Profit Factor:         {profit_factor:.2f}")
        
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 10: Return structured results
        result = {
            'strategy_name': strategy_class.__name__,
            'symbol': symbol,
            'start_date': start_date,
            'end_date': end_date,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio'),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': total_trades,
            'win_rate': win_rate,
            'profit_factor': profit_factor,
            'strategy_params': strategy_params or {}
        }
        
        return result

This is an important architectural decision. Let me help you think through it.
The Key Question: Integration vs. Separation?
You have two options:
Option A: Separate Project (Recommended)
Keep this AI research system completely separate from your existing trading code.
Pros:

✅ Clean separation of concerns
✅ Won't accidentally break your existing trading setup
✅ Can experiment freely without risk
✅ Easier to version control separately
✅ Different dependencies won't conflict
✅ Can share/backup this project independently

Cons:

❌ Code duplication if you want to test existing strategies
❌ Two separate folders to manage

Structure:
D:\
├── YourExistingTradingFolder\
│   ├── (your current trading code)
│   ├── (live trading scripts)
│   └── (whatever you have now)
│
└── TradingResearch\          ← NEW, separate project
    ├── strategies\           ← Research strategies
    ├── results\
    ├── data\
    └── backtester.py

Option B: Integrated Project
Put the AI research system inside your existing trading folder.
Pros:

✅ Everything in one place
✅ Can easily reference existing strategies
✅ Shared data folder
✅ One place to look for all trading code

Cons:

❌ Risk of mixing experimental code with production code
❌ Could accidentally modify working strategies
❌ Dependencies might conflict
❌ Harder to keep research separate from live trading

Structure:
D:\YourExistingTradingFolder\
├── (your existing files)
├── live_trading\
├── backtests\
├── ai_research\              ← NEW subfolder
│   ├── mutation_agent\
│   ├── backtester_agent\
│   ├── results\
│   └── generated_strategies\
└── shared_components\

My Strong Recommendation: Option A (Separate)
Here's why:
1. Different Purposes
Your existing folder:

Production/live trading code
Battle-tested strategies
Real money on the line
Stability is critical

This AI research system:

Experimental
Generates hundreds of untested variants
Rapid iteration
Breaking things is expected

These should not mix.
2. Risk Management
Imagine this scenario:

The Mutation Agent generates 200 strategy variants
One has a bug and overwrites a file
Suddenly your live trading strategy stops working
You're scrambling to figure out what changed

Separation = Safety
3. You Can Still Share Code
Even with separate projects, you can:
Import strategies from your main folder:
python# In D:\TradingResearch\test_existing_strategy.py

import sys
sys.path.append('D:/YourMainTradingFolder')

from your_strategies import YourExistingStrategy

Copy strategies you want to research:

Share data folders:

## Hybrid Approach (Best of Both Worlds)

Here's what I actually recommend:

### Structure:
```
D:\
├── YourMainTradingFolder\
│   ├── live_trading\
│   ├── strategies\           ← Your production strategies
│   ├── data\                 ← Shared historical data
│   └── utils\                ← Shared utilities
│
└── TradingResearch\          ← Separate AI research project
    ├── strategies\           ← Copies of strategies to research
    ├── generated_variants\   ← AI-generated strategies
    ├── results\              ← Research results database
    ├── backtester.py
    └── config.py             ← Points to shared data folder
In config.py:
python# config.py
import os

# Point to your main trading data folder (shared)
SHARED_DATA_FOLDER = "D:/YourMainTradingFolder/data"

# Point to your main strategies (for reference)
PRODUCTION_STRATEGIES_FOLDER = "D:/YourMainTradingFolder/strategies"

# Research-specific folders (separate)
RESEARCH_STRATEGIES_FOLDER = "D:/TradingResearch/strategies"
GENERATED_VARIANTS_FOLDER = "D:/TradingResearch/generated_variants"
RESULTS_DATABASE = "D:/TradingResearch/results/backtest_results.db"
Workflow:
When you want to research an existing strategy:

Copy it to the research folder
Let AI generate variants
Test all variants
Find best performers
Then carefully integrate the winner back into your main folder

Example:
bash# Copy strategy to research
copy D:\MainTrading\strategies\my_momentum_strategy.py D:\TradingResearch\strategies\

# Run AI research system (generates 100 variants, tests them all)
python research_workflow.py

# Review results, find winner
# Manually copy the best variant back to main folder
copy D:\TradingResearch\generated_variants\variant_042.py D:\MainTrading\strategies\momentum_v2.py
```

python# config.py

# Where your main trading data lives (shared, don't duplicate)
SHARED_DATA_PATH = "D:/Trading/data"

# Where to look for strategies you want to research
SOURCE_STRATEGIES_PATH = "D:/Trading"

# Where AI research files live (separate)
RESEARCH_PATH = "D:/TradingResearch"
RESULTS_DB = "D:/TradingResearch/results/backtest_results.db"

# Import helper function
def import_strategy_from_main(strategy_name):
    """Import a strategy from your main trading folder"""
    import sys
    sys.path.insert(0, SOURCE_STRATEGIES_PATH)
    
    module = __import__('my_strategies')
    return getattr(module, strategy_name)

Decision Framework
Ask yourself:
Choose SEPARATE if:

✅ You have live trading code you can't risk breaking
✅ You want to experiment freely
✅ You're still learning and might make mistakes
✅ You want clean version control
✅ This describes most people ← You probably want this

Choose INTEGRATED if:

✅ You don't have production code running yet
✅ Everything is still experimental
✅ You're very organized and disciplined about file management
✅ You want absolutely everything in one place

Paste this code:

python# simple_strategy.py
# This is a BASE STRATEGY - the AI will generate variants from this

import backtrader as bt

class SimpleMovingAverageCrossover(bt.Strategy):
    """
    BASE STRATEGY: Moving Average Crossover
    
    This is your starting point. The Mutation Agent will:
    - Test different MA periods (5/20, 10/30, 20/50, etc.)
    - Add filters (ADX, volatility, volume)
    - Add stops (ATR, percentage, trailing)
    - Add confirmations (RSI, MACD, etc.)
    
    You write this ONCE, AI generates 100s of variants
    """
    
    params = (
        ('fast_period', 10),   # Fast moving average period
        ('slow_period', 30),   # Slow moving average period
    )
    
    def __init__(self):
        # Calculate the two moving averages
        self.fast_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.fast_period
        )
        self.slow_ma = bt.indicators.SimpleMovingAverage(
            self.data.close, 
            period=self.params.slow_period
        )
        
        # Crossover signal
        self.crossover = bt.indicators.CrossOver(self.fast_ma, self.slow_ma)
    
    def next(self):
        # This runs every day/candle
        
        if not self.position:  # Not in a trade
            if self.crossover > 0:  # Fast MA crossed above slow MA
                self.buy()
                
        else:  # In a trade
            if self.crossover < 0:  # Fast MA crossed below slow MA
                self.sell()

Save it (Ctrl+S)


File 2: Create the Backtester

In the Explorer sidebar, right-click in the empty space (not in any folder)
Click "New File"
Name it: backtester.py
Paste this code:

python# backtester.py
# The BACKTESTING ENGINE - runs any strategy you give it
# This file stays the same - it's your testing machine

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
import pandas as pd

class StrategyBacktester:
    """
    This is your testing machine.
    
    You give it:
    - A strategy (base or AI-generated variant)
    - A stock/crypto/forex symbol
    - Date range
    
    It gives you back:
    - Performance metrics
    - Trade analysis
    - Risk statistics
    """
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=10000, commission=0.001, strategy_params=None):
        """
        Run a backtest
        
        Parameters:
        -----------
        strategy_class : class
            The strategy to test (e.g., SimpleMovingAverageCrossover)
        symbol : str
            Ticker symbol (e.g., 'AAPL', 'BTC-USD', 'EURUSD=X')
        start_date : str
            Start date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        end_date : str
            End date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        initial_cash : float
            Starting capital (default: $10,000)
        commission : float
            Trading fee per trade (default: 0.1% = 0.001)
        strategy_params : dict
            Custom parameters for the strategy (optional)
        
        Returns:
        --------
        dict : Backtest results with all metrics
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"BACKTESTING: {symbol}")
        print(f"Strategy: {strategy_class.__name__}")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"Starting Capital: ${initial_cash:,.2f}")
        if strategy_params:
            print(f"Parameters: {strategy_params}")
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 1: Download historical data
        print(f"📊 Downloading data for {symbol}...")
        try:
            data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Error downloading data: {e}")
            return None
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"❌ No data found for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        print(f"✓ Downloaded {len(data)} days of data")
        
        # Step 2: Create backtrader engine
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Step 3: Add data
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(dataname=data)
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Step 4: Add strategy (with custom params if provided)
        if strategy_params:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class, **strategy_params)
        else:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Step 5: Configure broker
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Step 6: Add analyzers (calculate performance metrics)
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.Returns, _name='returns')
        
        # Step 7: Run the backtest
        print(f"🔄 Running backtest...")
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        try:
            results = cerebro.run()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Backtest failed: {e}")
            return None
        
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Step 8: Extract results
        strat = results[0]
        
        # Get analyzer results
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        returns = strat.analyzers.returns.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate metrics
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        total_trades = trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0
        
        # Win rate
        win_rate = None
        if total_trades > 0:
            wins = trades.won.total if hasattr(trades, 'won') else 0
            win_rate = (wins / total_trades) * 100
        
        # Profit factor
        profit_factor = None
        if hasattr(trades, 'won') and hasattr(trades, 'lost'):
            gross_profit = trades.won.pnl.total if trades.won.pnl.total else 0
            gross_loss = abs(trades.lost.pnl.total) if trades.lost.pnl.total else 0
            if gross_loss > 0:
                profit_factor = gross_profit / gross_loss
        
        # Step 9: Print results
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"RESULTS FOR {symbol}")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print(f"Starting Portfolio:    ${starting_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Ending Portfolio:      ${ending_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Total Return:          {total_return:+.2f}%")
        print(f"Sharpe Ratio:          {sharpe.get('sharperatio', 'N/A')}")
        print(f"Max Drawdown:          {drawdown.max.drawdown:.2f}%")
        print(f"Total Trades:          {total_trades}")
        
        if win_rate is not None:
            print(f"Win Rate:              {win_rate:.2f}%")
        if profit_factor is not None:
            print(f"Profit Factor:         {profit_factor:.2f}")
        
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 10: Return structured results
        result = {
            'strategy_name': strategy_class.__name__,
            'symbol': symbol,
            'start_date': start_date,
            'end_date': end_date,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio'),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': total_trades,
            'win_rate': win_rate,
            'profit_factor': profit_factor,
            'strategy_params': strategy_params or {}
        }
        
        return result

Save it (Ctrl+S)

python# test_backtest.py
# PHASE 1 TEST - Verify the backtester works with your base strategy

from backtester import StrategyBacktester
from strategies.simple_strategy import SimpleMovingAverageCrossover

print("\n" + "="*70)
print("PHASE 1: BASIC BACKTEST TEST")

# Test 1: Basic test on Apple
print("\n📍 TEST 1: Apple (AAPL) - 2020 to 2023")
result = backtester.run_backtest(
    strategy_class=SimpleMovingAverageCrossover,
    symbol='AAPL',
    start_date='2020-01-01',
    end_date='2023-12-31',
    initial_cash=10000,
    commission=0.001
)

if result:
    print("✅ Test 1 PASSED - Backtester works!")
else:
    print("❌ Test 1 FAILED - Check errors above")
    exit()

# Test 2: Test with custom parameters
print("\n📍 TEST 2: Same strategy with different parameters")
print("            (Testing 20/50 day moving averages instead of 10/30)")

result2 = backtester.run_backtest(
    strategy_class=SimpleMovingAverageCrossover,
    symbol='AAPL',
    start_date='2020-01-01',
    end_date='2023-12-31',
    initial_cash=10000,
    commission=0.001,
    strategy_params={'fast_period': 20, 'slow_period': 50}  # Different parameters
)

if result2:
    print("✅ Test 2 PASSED - Parameter customization works!")
    
    # Compare the two
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("COMPARISON: 10/30 MA vs 20/50 MA")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"10/30 MA Return: {result['total_return_pct']:+.2f}%")
    print(f"20/50 MA Return: {result2['total_return_pct']:+.2f}%")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
else:
    print("❌ Test 2 FAILED")
    exit()

print("\n" + "="*70)
print("✅ PHASE 1 COMPLETE!")
print("="*70)
print("\nYour backtesting engine is working correctly.")
print("\nNext steps:")
print("  → Phase 2: Add database storage")
print("  → Phase 3: Integrate Claude AI for analysis")
print("  → Phase 4: Build the Mutation Agent")
print("\nThe Mutation Agent will automatically generate variants like:")
print("  • 5/15 MA, 10/30 MA, 20/50 MA (different periods)")
print("  • MA + ADX filter")
print("  • MA + RSI confirmation")
print("  • MA + ATR stops")
print("  • ...and hundreds more")
print("="*70 + "\n")

Fix 2: Update the backtester to handle the new yfinance format
Replace your backtester.py with this updated version (it fixes the column name issue):
python# backtester.py
# The BACKTESTING ENGINE - runs any strategy you give it
# This file stays the same - it's your testing machine

import backtrader as bt
import yfinance as yf
import pandas as pd

class StrategyBacktester:
    """
    This is your testing machine.
    
    You give it:
    - A strategy (base or AI-generated variant)
    - A stock/crypto/forex symbol
    - Date range
    
    It gives you back:
    - Performance metrics
    - Trade analysis
    - Risk statistics
    """
    
    def run_backtest(self, strategy_class, symbol, start_date, end_date, 
                     initial_cash=10000, commission=0.001, strategy_params=None):
        """
        Run a backtest
        
        Parameters:
        -----------
        strategy_class : class
            The strategy to test (e.g., SimpleMovingAverageCrossover)
        symbol : str
            Ticker symbol (e.g., 'AAPL', 'BTC-USD', 'EURUSD=X')
        start_date : str
            Start date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        end_date : str
            End date 'YYYY-MM-DD'
        initial_cash : float
            Starting capital (default: $10,000)
        commission : float
            Trading fee per trade (default: 0.1% = 0.001)
        strategy_params : dict
            Custom parameters for the strategy (optional)
        
        Returns:
        --------
        dict : Backtest results with all metrics
        """
        
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"BACKTESTING: {symbol}")
        print(f"Strategy: {strategy_class.__name__}")
        print(f"Period: {start_date} to {end_date}")
        print(f"Starting Capital: ${initial_cash:,.2f}")
        if strategy_params:
            print(f"Parameters: {strategy_params}")
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 1: Download historical data
        print(f"📊 Downloading data for {symbol}...")
        try:
            data = yf.download(symbol, start=start_date, end=end_date, progress=False)
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Error downloading data: {e}")
            return None
        
        if data.empty:
            print(f"❌ No data found for {symbol}")
            return None
        
        # FIX: Flatten multi-level column headers if present
        if isinstance(data.columns, pd.MultiIndex):
            data.columns = data.columns.get_level_values(0)
        
        # FIX: Ensure column names are strings and lowercase
        data.columns = [str(col).lower() for col in data.columns]
        
        print(f"✓ Downloaded {len(data)} days of data")
        
        # Step 2: Create backtrader engine
        cerebro = bt.Cerebro()
        
        # Step 3: Add data with explicit column mapping
        data_feed = bt.feeds.PandasData(
            dataname=data,
            datetime=None,  # Use index as datetime
            open='open',
            high='high',
            low='low',
            close='close',
            volume='volume',
            openinterest=-1  # Not used
        )
        cerebro.adddata(data_feed)
        
        # Step 4: Add strategy (with custom params if provided)
        if strategy_params:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class, **strategy_params)
        else:
            cerebro.addstrategy(strategy_class)
        
        # Step 5: Configure broker
        cerebro.broker.setcash(initial_cash)
        cerebro.broker.setcommission(commission=commission)
        
        # Step 6: Add analyzers (calculate performance metrics)
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.SharpeRatio, _name='sharpe')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.DrawDown, _name='drawdown')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.TradeAnalyzer, _name='trades')
        cerebro.addanalyzer(bt.analyzers.Returns, _name='returns')
        
        # Step 7: Run the backtest
        print(f"🔄 Running backtest...")
        starting_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        try:
            results = cerebro.run()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"❌ Backtest failed: {e}")
            import traceback
            traceback.print_exc()
            return None
        
        ending_value = cerebro.broker.getvalue()
        
        # Step 8: Extract results
        strat = results[0]
        
        # Get analyzer results
        sharpe = strat.analyzers.sharpe.get_analysis()
        drawdown = strat.analyzers.drawdown.get_analysis()
        trades = strat.analyzers.trades.get_analysis()
        returns = strat.analyzers.returns.get_analysis()
        
        # Calculate metrics
        total_return = ((ending_value - starting_value) / starting_value) * 100
        total_trades = trades.total.closed if trades.total.closed else 0
        
        # Win rate
        win_rate = None
        if total_trades > 0:
            wins = trades.won.total if hasattr(trades, 'won') else 0
            win_rate = (wins / total_trades) * 100
        
        # Profit factor
        profit_factor = None
        if hasattr(trades, 'won') and hasattr(trades, 'lost'):
            gross_profit = trades.won.pnl.total if trades.won.pnl.total else 0
            gross_loss = abs(trades.lost.pnl.total) if trades.lost.pnl.total else 0
            if gross_loss > 0:
                profit_factor = gross_profit / gross_loss
        
        # Step 9: Print results
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"RESULTS FOR {symbol}")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print(f"Starting Portfolio:    ${starting_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Ending Portfolio:      ${ending_value:,.2f}")
        print(f"Total Return:          {total_return:+.2f}%")
        print(f"Sharpe Ratio:          {sharpe.get('sharperatio', 'N/A')}")
        print(f"Max Drawdown:          {drawdown.max.drawdown:.2f}%")
        print(f"Total Trades:          {total_trades}")
        
        if win_rate is not None:
            print(f"Win Rate:              {win_rate:.2f}%")
        if profit_factor is not None:
            print(f"Profit Factor:         {profit_factor:.2f}")
        
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Step 10: Return structured results
        result = {
            'strategy_name': strategy_class.__name__,
            'symbol': symbol,
            'start_date': start_date,
            'end_date': end_date,
            'starting_value': starting_value,
            'ending_value': ending_value,
            'total_return_pct': total_return,
            'sharpe_ratio': sharpe.get('sharperatio'),
            'max_drawdown_pct': drawdown.max.drawdown,
            'total_trades': total_trades,
            'win_rate': win_rate,
            'profit_factor': profit_factor,
            'strategy_params': strategy_params or {}
        }
        
        return result
